REPUBLIC OF THE GAMBIA
WOMEN IN DEVELOPMENT PROJECT
COMPONENT FOR STRENGTHENING OF THE WOMEN'S BUREAU
1.        The objective of this component is to strengthen the capacity of
the Women's Bureau for policy and program formulation, advice, awareness
creation, and monitoring and evaluation of the impact of women's
development programs. The strategy envisaged includes changes in the
Bureau's organizational structure and staffing, the training of staff, and
the provision of technical assistance, as well as investments in a new
headquarters building, furniture, equipment and vehicles. The component
consists of two sub-components: general strengthening of the Bureau, and
monitoring and evaluation.
A. General Strengthening of the Women's Bureau
2.        This sub-component continues and expands on the assistance
currently provided by UNIFEM, and includes the following:
a.   Reinforcement of the Research Unit through the provision of a
researcher and social scientist; the unit's research program
would focus on small-scale and special surveys to supplement
national data programs.
b.   Some decentralization of the Bureau's activities throurh the
work of field officers (6 women and 5 men), the training of
women leaders, and the setting up of meetings, workshops and
seminars in the Regions in order to expand the outreach to
women, gain a better understanding of their needs, and
facilitate the collection of data and information for research.
c.   Strengthening of the Bureau's capability to collaborate and
negotiate with other agencies, to ensure that their programs
include women-oriented activities, through the provision of two
planners.
d.   Improvement of the Bureau's documentation and reference service
through the provision of a documentalist and documentation and
subscriptions.
e.   Enhancement of the Bureau's communications program through the
provision of an editor and of funds for producing publications,
including a newsletter.
f.   A new headquarters building for the Bureau, together with
furniture and equipment, and vehicles for the Bureau's staff
plus funds for o'"erations and maintenance.
3.        The Research Unit should be able to provide both basic research
on the situation of women in The Gambia and applied research of direct



- 100 -                          LNNEX 3-5
Page 2 of 9
relevance to the VID project. Research topics being considered include:
traditional practices affecting the role, status and material circumstances
of Gambian women, their contribution to food production, health problems,
access to credit and technology, and business and employment opportunities.
Priorities need to be established and proposals prepared for the research
projects that should be undertaken first.  In view of the manpower
shortage, it is advisable to group the research topics and limit the
proposals to a few of special interest for the WID project   For instance,
these may be on (a) gender relationships in rural households, with a focus
on agriculture and food production; and (b) health-care practices and
beliefs (traditional and modern), including health services delivery and
food preparation practices. Research in these fields should combine macro-
level surveys with in-depth, holistic studies in limited areas (a few
representative villages) based on qualitative methods and analysis. This
approach would not only provide an answer to the question of how a
particular phenomenon, opinion or practice is disseminated within a
populiatikn, but also may show how registered social patterns have come
about. Such qualitative studies proviae more useful knowledge and are
cheaper to implement, requiring less manpower than quantitative studies,
although they require a somewhat longer time in the field. As the Bureau
needs the assistance of a consultant to formulate an appropriate research
program, technical assistance (one person-month) has been provided for that
purpose under the PPF.
4.        The head of the Research Unit should be knowledgeable about
qualitative as well as quantitative methods and analysis, and preferably
should be a social anthropologist or rural sociologist. Consultants and
outside evaluators would be utilized, but the Unit would also be
strengthened by providing a social scientist. It would be useful to
encourage Gambians studying abroad for a social sciences degree to do some
of the field work for their thesis as part of the Bureau's research
program.
5.        The existing offices of the Women's Bureau are not adequate and
need expensive repairs and renovations that would not be cost-effective.
Therefore, the construction of a new headquarters building is justified,
subject to agreement being reached on the appropriate size, standards and
cost of the building and on the availability of a suitable site. A firm of
architects/engineers should be hired to prepare plans, specifications, cost
estimates and bidding documents, and at a later stage to supervise
construction. Since a local firm could do this work, local technical
assistance (7-1/2 person-months) has been provided under the PPF for the
design of the headquarters building and for the preparation of bidding
documents.
6.        Research and frequent progrrm evaluations are extremely
important to detect at an early stage any unintended consequences of
programs and ensure that the particular target group actually benefits. In
light of this linkage between research and evaluation, the Bureau's
Research and Monitoring and Evaluation Units should work closely together.
At mid-point during project implementation there should be an assessment of
the possibility of merging the two units.



- 101 -                         ANNEX 3-5
Page 3 of 9
B. Monitoring and Evaluation
7.        A Monitoring and Evaluation (M&E) Unit will be established
within the Women's Bureau. Initially, its main functions will be to
provide the Project Management Unit (PHU) with relevant and timely
information for the monitoring of the WID project and to measure its
impact. As the Unit develops its capabilities and gains more experience,
it will also assume responsibility for monitoring and evaluating other
women's development programs and projecus.
8.        The design of the M&E system for the WID project is tased on the
concept of a logical framework for the project, i.e., its hierarchy of
objectives. Each project activity or component can be seen as requiring
certain resources and achieving certain results. First, each component
requires a supply of physical, financial and staff inputs, the use of which
leads to specific project outputs; these, in turn, achieve certain
immediate effects, either intended or unintended, on the target population.
In due course the effects accumulate to produce an overall level of impact,
which if project intervention works as intended, contributes to the overall
development objectives. This four-tier hierarchy of inputs, outputs,
effects and impact provides a systematic way of viewing the many objectives
and tasks of this multi-component project, as well as a logical structure
for management ts. plan, execute and monitor them. At each level of the
hierarchy a set of minimum objectives can be defined and appropriate
indicators selected to determine whether or not they have been reached.
The success of the various components can be measured and reported on
regularly through the use of such carefully chosen indicators.
9.        As monitorinx provides . continuous assessment of the
functioning of project activities and of the use of project inputs in the
context of implementation schedules and design expectations, the M&E Unit
would help management to implement the project by (a) designing and
organizing a regular and timely flow of relevant data and information; (b)
analyzing the information to check whether pre-set goals are being achieved
and to assess the extent to which the project has successfully translated
the physical and financial resources made available to it into the intended
activities; and (c) identifying the reasons for any delays or constraints
that may arise.
10.       Considering the nature of the WID project, monitoring would be
the responsibility of each of the agencies responsible for implementing its
components or sub-components, as an essential part of the management of
their specific activities. The H&E Unit would coordinate the monitoring
activities of the various component agencies and collate and interpret the
information they provide. In collaboration with all of the agencies and
ministries involved in project implementation, the M&E Unit would design
and institute a monitoring system based on periodic reporting of a number
of key indicators of project operations and performance. These indicators
would be compared with the physical and financial targets set annually in
the work plan and budget prepared by t'.e PMU and approved by the Project
Coordinating Committee (PCC). All project agencies and ministries involved



- 102 -                          ANNEX 3-5
Page 4 of 9
in implementation would be responsible for submitting to the M&E Unit the
required information on a quarterly, seasonal or annual basis, as
appropriate.
11.       The August 30, 1989, consultants' reports on monitoring and
evaluation and the September 1989 report of the Consolidation Workshop for
the WID Proiect contain lists of proposed indicators of inputs and outputs
for each project component. These lists should be reviewed in detail and,
if necessary, revised by the management of each component or sub-component
in collaboration with the M&E Unit and the PMU which will specify the type
and frequency of information required. Having selected the most appropriate
indicators, the component managers should attach to them quantified targets
on a quarterly, annual or seasonal basis to match the reporting schedules
and work plan.
12.       The M&E Unit would also carry out these activities necessary for
evaluation of project effectiveness and, to the extent possible, the
project's impact in the context of its stated objectives. These activities
would also involve the full collaboration of both the monitoring staff and
the management of each implemp"ting agency, being primarily designed to
meet the information needs of management. Since the objective of
evaluation is to assess the extent to which the project activities or
outputs have reached the defined target population and achieved the
intended impact, it provides a basis for corrective action, if necessary,
during project implementation, as well as for ex-post evaluation.
13.       The August 30, 1989, consultant's report on M&E and the
September 1989 report of the Consolidation Workshop also contain lists of
proposed project effects and impact indicators for each component. A
Baseline Survey, a Knowledge, Attitudes and Practices (KAP) Survey, and
Project Services Monitoring Surveys would be undertaken to cover the main
data collection requirements for those indicators, revised, when necessary,
by the M&E Unit in collaboration with the management of each component.
14.       The Baseline Survey, as a key element in the M&E design for the
WID project, would focus on women living in the 200 villages where the
majority of project activities would be concentrated. These women comprise
the project's primary target population, although some of its aspects
would also have a nationwide impact. The purpose of the survey is to
provide:
(a) A set of representative and contemporary information on the
demographic, agricultural, social and economic characteristics
of the target population.
(b) An empirical framework that can serve to confirm the importance
of key project initiatives (e.g. savings mobilization, input
distribution, extension services, skills development, and
improved healthprogram) and the relative emphasis to be placed
on each of these in       selected villages.



- 103 -                          ANNEX 3-5
Page 5 of 9
(c) Agricultural, education and health related data on the situation
of women that can be used in the design of the project
components.
(d) The first, ex-ante set of data in a phased series of
investigations designed to provide a way to assess changes in
the circumstances of women. In conjunction with the findings of
the component-specific surveys to be undertaken during project
implementation, the KAP Survey and the Social Dimension of
AdJustment (SDA) Household Survey Program, the Baseline Survey
should ultimately give an indication of the overall socio-
economic changes resulting from the project.
15.       The Baseline Survey, concentrating on the 200 target villages
(para 14), would use this village list as its sampling framework.
Respcndents would be women residents (aged 15 years or more) in the target
villages. The respondents would only be women because the aim is to gain
factual information about the target beneficiaries and it is assumed there
is no information about women's activities that could be better supplied by
men. A sample of 50 of the 200 project villages is proposed, with a
maximum of Six women interviewed per village, making a total of 300. While
one could argue for a larger sample s'.ze, the survey planned could easily
over-extend ti. capacity of the M&E Unit, and therefore the size of the
sample should be kept as small as possible. A final decision would have to
be made after the survey questionnaire has been revised and again tested in
the field. Elements of the survey, particularly those related to basic
socio-economic parameters, would be repeated at mid-term, at the end of the
project, and two years after project completion. Other parts of the survey
would be modified at each of these intervals to better achieve the key
objective of measuring any improvement in the circumstances of women in the
light of the project activities that have taken place. Insofar as
possible, the same respondents would be interviewed each time the survey is
repeated. The ultimate goal is to produce a descriptive series of data
reflecting the living and working conditions of women and their knowledge
and practices over a period of seven years. To the extent that these
changes can be related to project activities in the context of the overall
monitoring program, an estimate of project effects and impact can be made.
16.       The Knowledte. Attitudes and Practices (KAP) Survey would
complement the Baseline Survey and support the information, education and
comunnication (IEC) component. This survey would use a probability sample
drawn from the whole population, including women and men. Its purpose is
to provide:
(a) A set of representative and contemporary information on
the knowledge, attitudes and pra-tices of the population
with regard to the status and situation of women and the
most important gender issues.
(b) Empirical data that can be used to assist in designing the IEC
component, particularly the messages that should be



- 104 -                          ANNEX 3-5
Page 6 of 9
transmitted, the media used, and the emphasis given to the materials
relevant to each project component.
(c)  An initial survey ("ex-ante') which, when repeated during   or
after project implementatioii, would provide a way to assess the
success of the project in changing the awareness and attitudes of the
population with regard to the circumstances of women; also, the
extent to which working, domestic and harmful traditional practices
have improved.
17.       For the same reasons as for the Baseline Survey, it is proposed
that the sample size for the KAP Survey should be 300, with six respondents
to be selected within each enumeratien area; 50% of them should be female
and 50% male. Interviewing men is important, because their attitudes and
practices may constrain women's opportunities for improvement. The
questionnaire already prepared needs to be revised and again tested in the
field. The survey would be repeated at mid-term and at the end of the
project to measure any changes in awareness and practices that may have
taken place as a result of the project. Owing to the sensitive nature of
some of the questions, an effort should be made to ensure anonymity of the
respondents and a new sample would be drawn each time the survey is
repeated. This approach is more appropriate for this type of survey, which
resembles market research investigations, and for which repeated interviews
may themselves influence the attitudes of the respondents.
18.       The Proiect Services -onitoring Surveys would be small-scale, ad
hoc surveys designed to achieve particular objectives. They would be used
primarily to monitor the effects and impact of those project sub-components
that involve extension to women of improved practices, education and
training; these include, for example, the crop production, horticultural
and livestock extension activities of the agricultural component, the
numeracy/literacy and other skills training of the skills development
component, and the family planning and nutrition education activities of
the safe motherhood and FP component.
19.       These surveys will use a 'market research" approach to provide
information on whether the services are reaching women (beneficiary
contacts) and whether they meet the women's needs (adoption rate of the
recommendations). To be useful to management for timely decision-making,
the surveys should produce regular and timely information and results
sufficiently disaggregated to allow managers to compare farmers' responses
in different areas; they should also be capable of distinguishing among
women used as change agents, as group leaders or as contacts in the
extension process, and other women not directly contacted.
20.       To satisfy these requirements, the surveys should be kept short
and simple, aiming for a minimum workload, and be a routine component of
project monitoring, conducted at least annually. The actual timing of the
surveys would depend on the nature of the project services provided in any
given period. The sampling framework for the surveys would be women
residents in a number of the target villages included in a particular



- 105 -                          ANNEX 3-5
Page 7 of 9
extension campaign. An appropriate sample size would be 50-70 women in
total.
21.       It would not be possible for the M&E Unit alone to implement all
surveys of this nature, nor is it desirable that it do so. Hence, the
surveys should be designed jointly with the implementing agencies
responsible for particular extension campaigns. Data collection should
preferably be carried out by the supervisors of those campaigns, with
enumerators seconded from the M&E Unit, as required. The M&E officer and
assistants of the M&E Unit would assist in the design and implementation of
such surveys and also perform a quality-control function. They would
jointly carry out the survey analyses and preparation of the necessary
reports with the staff of the extension agency.
22.       Diagnostic studies may also be required when specific
implementation problems are identified during M&E activities. These should
be organized in a similar fashion as the Project Services Monitoring
Surveys, though they are likely to commence with an initial appraisal of
the situation by senior evaluation and technical staff.
23.       The impact evaluation proaram should be an integrated program,
using both primary and secondary sources of data. The entire program is
designed to be compatible with and to make use of other data-collection
activities that will proceed in parallel in The Gambia, particularly the
SDA Household Survey Program and the National Agricultural Sample Survey.
The SDA Household Survey Program includes a Priority Survey to be carried
out during the second half of 1990, and an Intensive Survey and a Community
Survey in 1991, to gather complementary and disaggregated socio-economic
data at different levels. The SDA program will also help strengthen the
Women's Bureau through the provision of a vehicle, equipment, staff
training, and a WID specialist (sociologist) for the Research Unit.
24.       The M&E Unit would be headed by an M&E officer, with
responsibility for implementation of the survey programs and the collation
of all WID project monitoring data for the PMU. The M&E officer would be
responsible to the Executive Secretary of the Women's Bureau and liaise
closely with the WID Project Manager. Under the M&E officer would be two
full-time monitoring and evaluation assistants. Their primary task would
be to assist the M&E officer in the compilation of WID project progress
reports and to supervise primary data-collection activities. They would
also assist in evaluating the Bureau's other projects and programs, as and
when requested by its other units. One assistant should be given
particular responsibility for the M&E Unit's computing facilities, the
processing of survey data, and management of the data base. The other
assistant should be responsible for supervising field work and the training
and management of enumerators. Despite this division of responsibilities,
both assistants should receive training in computing and survey
methodologies to allow them to share the workload at times of peak
activity.
25.       This sub-component's cost includes the costs of a vehicle,
computing facilities and equipment, staff training, technical assistance,



- 106 -                          ANNEX 3-5
Page 8 of 9
surveys, the personal costs of the M&E officer and the two assistants, and
the M&E Unit's operating costs. The sub-component includes the provision
of an internationally recruited M&E consultant (7 person/months) whose
periodic inputs would include technical guidance and support for
computerized data processing and analysis, the final detailed design of the
monitoring system, project services monitoring surveys, diagnostic studies
design and analysis, and the final evaluation study. The objective is to
provide the M&E Unit with the capability to design, process and analyze its
primary data collection activities.
26.       An M&E Coordination Committee, chaired by the WID Project
Manager and with the Women's Bureau M&E officer as Secretary, would be
established to coordinate the design and activities of the various
monitoring and evaluation systems and the dissemination of information.
The Committee would be composed of the coordinator or senior manager of
each of the project components and the person in each component with
responsibility for overall monitoring. NGOs responsible for implementing
project activities should also be represented.
27.       Before commencement of the project, the M&E Committee should
meet monthly to review plans for a Progress Reporting System. The detailed
design of this system for each project component should be prepared by the
component implementing agencies, with support from the M&E Unit. The lists
of indicators (paras 11-13) provide a starting point for designing the
system. The component implementing agencies should finalize their
respective lists of indicators and attach realistic targets to each one,
against which actual progress can be measured; for most indicators,
quarterly implementation targets should be required. The M&E Committee
should agree on a schedule for the submission of progress reports to the
M&E Unit and the key indicators to be reported. It is suggested that after
project co"mencement most of the indicators of project inputs and outputs
should be reported on a quarterly basis. The Committee should then also
meet on a quarterly basis to review the findings of the monitoring system
and the reasons for any delays in report submission. Plans for the
progress reporting system should be finalized and reviewed at the workshop
to be held to assess the results of the Baseline and KAP Surveys (see para
29 below).
28.       Standard reporting formats should be developed within each
component and for submission to the M&E Unit insofar as possible. This
may, however, be difficult in the short term owing to the diverse nature
and, in some cases, staggered implementation of some of the sub-components.
All progress reports should establish the current status of the activities
being monitored and the accomplishments of the work program. The progress
re-orted should always be compared with what was planned, and any current
or potential problems should be discussed. Each progress report should
review all activities in the work program for the particular period.
29.       Funds have been provided under the PPF to carry out the Baseline
Survey and the KAP Survey before the start of the project. A one-week
workshop should be held following completion of the analysis of the first
round of the Baseline and KAP Surveys to present their findings.



- 107 -                          ANNEX 35-
Page 9 of 9
Participants should be invited from all project components and sub-
components. This workshop should also be used to explain fully the role of
the M&E Unit and to clear up any outstanding issues in the design of the
Progress Reporting System. Initial discussions should be held to identify
and commence plann:. ; of the first Project Service Monitoring Surveys. The
emphasis in the workshop should be on presenting the M&E Unit as a full
partner of the component implementing agencies. The workshop should be
held annually, with a similar format and timed to review the results of any
survey investigations carried out following the rainy season.



ANNEX 3-6
- 108 -                        Page 1 of 4
REPUBLIC OF THE GAMBIA
WOMEN IN DEVELOPMENT PROJECT
THE FUND COMPONENT
1.        The Fund would assist in financing small projects or programs
designed to improve the living and/or working standards of women and
children in The Gambia, particularly those in the poorest and most
vulnerable groups. The project or program should be innovative and of high
developmental priority, and may include activities such as vegetable
gardening, well-digging, soap production, pottery-making, sewing,
establishment of an ice plant, and other innovative activities that address
the urgent needs of these vulnerable groups.
2.        The proceeds of the Fund would be made available, as grants and
on a matching basis, to eligible non-governmental organizations (NGOs) for
purposes of the projects or programs referred to above. The matching funds
to be provided by an NGO from its own and other non-Fund sources should be
at least 25X of the total cost of the project or program.
3.        The following criteria would be applied in determining the
eligibility of an NGO to receive grants from the Fund:
(a) The NGO must be registered with the Government of The
Gambia in accordance with the applicable laws and
regulations;
(b) The NGO must be able to contribute the 25? matching funds
referred to in para 2 above;
(c) The NGO must have a good knowledge of the local situations
and demonstrate (i) a proven institutional track record,
and (ii) a work program in which the proposal submitted by
the NGO is well integrated;
(d) The proposal must (i) show all costs to be covered from
sources other than the Fund; (ii) identify those other
sources; and (iii) include reasonable estimates of the
value of in-kind contributions to be made by the NGO in the
estimates of the total cost of the project or program and
the NGO's contribution to such costs;
(e) The proposal should (i) aim at improving the living and/or
working standards of the project or program beneficiaries,
who should comprise the poorest and most vulnerable groups;
and (ii) be action-oriented and demonstrate an innovative
approach to addressing the issues of women in development,



- 109 -                          ANNEX 3-6
Page 2 of 4
such an innovative approach to include replication in a new
geographical area or areas of an innovative approach
already tested in one place;
(f) The proposal should (i) identify any existing kafos within
the project or program area; (ii) describe the activities
of such kafos; and (iii) show how the project or program
would work with their activities;
(g) The proposal should (i) be technically feasible,
justifiable and appropriate to the social and cultural
environment, and be manageable by beneficiaries
participating in carrying it out; (ii) identify the
recurrent cost requirements to be generated by the project
or program; (iii) show how these costs would be met; and
(iv) to the extent practicable, reflect the active
participation of beneficiaries in the design of the project
or program;
(h) If it involves training and research, the proposal should
(i) identify the necessary follow-up action as an integral
part of the project or program; (ii) where the training
involves the acquisition of skills of any kind, demonstrate
how the beneficiaries of such training would be expected to
use the acquired skills; and (iii) describe the methods of
procuring any necessary training and/or research materials;
(i) The proposal should identify (i) the owners of any
equipment, materials, building or land to be provided under
the project or program, and (ii) the measures to be taken
to ensure that ownership of such equipment, materials,
buildings or land resides exclusively with the
beneficiaries of the project or program and not,
opportunistically, with any other individual, groups,
organizations or village;
(j) The proposal should (i) specify how the project or program
would relate to available government services in the
project or program area; and (ii) identify all in-kind
resources within the project or program and, to the extent
practicable, estimate their value and show the different
sources of such in-kind resources; and
(k) The proposal should include a monitoring and evaluation
plan compatible with the monitoring and evaluation programs
of the relevant sectoral components of the proposed WID
project to which the project or program relates.
4.        The Fund would be administered by the Project Management Unit
(PMU) of the WID project in accordance with procedures satisfactory to
IDA, including the following:



- 110 -                          ANNEX 3-6
Page 3 of 4
(a) An NGO wishing to apply for a grant from the Fund should
furnish to the PMU, with a copy to the Chairman of the
Project Coordinating Committee (PCC), its project or
program proposal.
(b) PMU's ProJect Manager should promptly review every such
proposal in the light of the criteria described in para 3
above, and not later than two weeks after receipt of any
such proposal, transmit to the PCC the PMU's written
recommendations on the proposal.
(c) The PCC should promptly consider the PMU's recommendations
and approve or deny the application for the grant, giving
in every case of denial, in writing, the PCC's reasons for
denying the application.
(d) As soon as possible after the application for a grant has
been approved, the PMU and the NGO concerned should enter
into an agreement, the terms and conditions of which shall
have been approved by IDA. This agreement should, inter
alia, require the NGO (i) to maintain separate records and
accounts adequate to reflect, in accordance with sound
accounting practices, the operations, resources and
expenditures of the NGO in respect of the project or
program to be financed from proceeds of the grant made
available to the NGO; (ii) permit these records and
accounts to be audited by the auditors required to audit
the records and accounts of the Ministries, departments,
and agencies of the Government participating in the WID
project at the times and in the manner required under the
Development Credit Agreement (Women in Development Project)
to be entered into between the Government and IDA; (iii)
procure goods, works and services to be financed out of the
proceeds of any such grant at a reasonable price, account
also being taken of other relevant factors such as time of
delivery and efficiency and reliability of the goods and
availability of maintenance facilities and spare parts and,
in the case of services, of their quality and the
competence of the parties rendering them; and (iv) use such
goods, works and services exclusively for carrying out the
project or program.
(e) The maximum grant to any one NGO would not exceed in the
aggregate US$50,000 equivalent.
(f) The NGO to which a grant has been made should not later
than three months after the end of the first and the second
six-month period of the Government's fiscal year, furnish
semiannual reports, accompanied by statements of
expenditure, to the PMU showing progress in carrying out
the project or program financed from the grant.



ANNEX 3-6
Page 4 of 4
(g) The NGO to which a grant has been made should open an
account at a commercial bank, to which should be credited
the proceeds of the grant made available to the NGO for
purposes of the project or program and the matching
counterpart funds to be contributed by the NGO to the
project or program. The project account should be used
exclusively for expenditures to be made under the proJect
or program.
(h) The NGO should not later than three months &fter completion
of a project or program for which it has received a grant,
furnish to the PMU, with a copy to the PCC md to IDA, a
project or program completion report which, inter al1i,
states whether the objectives of the project or program for
which a grant has been made have been fulfilled.
